 Classes

Class: dnas:Actions   back to top

  • sted:H-BInteraction
    • dnas:Actions

NOTE dnas:Actions is a leaf node.

Description

Input an action ID,assign label, and give description in comment. For example, Action0001 labels as turning on the light. Moreover, it can be multiplt action such as turning on the light + openning window. - Actions are interactions with systems or activities that an occupant can conduct in order to satisfy their needs. The violation of one or more of an occupant's needs leads to discomfort. There- fore, this uncomfortable state for the occupant will provoke an action.
The action may be an interaction with a system in which the occupant conjectures that their action will restore comfort. - This class is associated with "State".

Class: expo:ConstantQuantity   back to top

  • expo:PhysicalQuantity
    • expo:ConstantQuantity

NOTE expo:ConstantQuantity is a leaf node.

Description


"A ConstantQuantity is a PhysicalQuantity which has a constant value, e.g. 3 meters and 5 hours. The magnitude (see MagnitudeFn) of every ConstantQuantity is a RealNumber. ConstantQuantities are distinguished from FunctionQuantities, which map ConstantQuantities to other ConstantQuantities. All ConstantQuantites are expressed with the BinaryFunction MeasureFn, which takes a Number and a UnitOfMeasure as arguments. For example, 3 Meters can be expressed as (MeasureFn 3 Meter). ConstantQuantities form a partial order (see PartialOrderingRelation) with the lessThan relation, since lessThan is a RelationExtendedToQuantities and lessThan is defined over the RealNumbers. The lessThan relation is not a total order (see TotalOrderingRelation) over the class ConstantQuantity since elements of some subclasses of ConstantQuantity (such as length quantities) are incomparable to elements of other subclasses of ConstantQuantity (such as mass quantities)." (SUMO)

Inherits from (4):
expo:PhysicalQuantity | expo:Quantity | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

Implementation:

@prefix expo: <http://www.hozo.jp/owl/EXPOApr19/> .
@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

expo:ConstantQuantity a owl:Class ;
rdfs:label "ConstantQuantity" ;
rdfs:comment """
"A ConstantQuantity is a PhysicalQuantity which has a constant value, e.g. 3 meters and 5 hours. The magnitude (see MagnitudeFn) of every ConstantQuantity is a RealNumber. ConstantQuantities are distinguished from FunctionQuantities, which map ConstantQuantities to other ConstantQuantities. All ConstantQuantites are expressed with the BinaryFunction MeasureFn, which takes a Number and a UnitOfMeasure as arguments. For example, 3 Meters can be expressed as (MeasureFn 3 Meter). ConstantQuantities form a partial order (see PartialOrderingRelation) with the lessThan relation, since lessThan is a RelationExtendedToQuantities and lessThan is defined over the RealNumbers. The lessThan relation is not a total order (see TotalOrderingRelation) over the class ConstantQuantity since elements of some subclasses of ConstantQuantity (such as length quantities) are incomparable to elements of other subclasses of ConstantQuantity (such as mass quantities)." (SUMO)
""" ;
rdfs:subClassOf expo:PhysicalQuantity ;
owl:disjointWith expo:TimeMeasure .

An experimental model is a description of dependencies (e.g. logical/mathematical) between experimental factors, others known variables, and unknown variables. "A PhysicalQuantity is a measure of some quantifiable aspect of the modeled world, such as 'the earth's diameter' (a constant length) and 'the stress in a loaded deformable solid' (a measure of stress, which is a function of three spatial coordinates). All PhysicalQuantities are either ConstantQuantities or FunctionQuantities. Instances of ConstantQuantity are dependent on a UnitOfMeasure, while instances of FunctionQuantity are Functions that map instances of ConstantQuantity to other instances of ConstantQuantity (e.g., TimeDependentQuantities are FunctionQuantities). Although the name and definition of PhysicalQuantity is borrowed from physics, PhysicalQuantities need not be material. Aside from the dimensions of length, time, velocity, etc., nonphysical dimensions such as currency are also possible. Accordingly, amounts of money would be instances of PhysicalQuantity. PhysicalQuantities are distinguished from Numbers by the fact that the former are associated with a dimension of measurement." SUMO: http://www.ontologyportal.org/

Inherits from (3):
expo:Quantity | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

Implementation:

@prefix expo: <http://www.hozo.jp/owl/EXPOApr19/> .
@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

expo:PhysicalQuantity a owl:Class ;
rdfs:label "PhysicalQuantity" ;
rdfs:comment """
"A PhysicalQuantity is a measure of some quantifiable aspect of the modeled world, such as 'the earth's diameter' (a constant length) and 'the stress in a loaded deformable solid' (a measure of stress, which is a function of three spatial coordinates). All PhysicalQuantities are either ConstantQuantities or FunctionQuantities. Instances of ConstantQuantity are dependent on a UnitOfMeasure, while instances of FunctionQuantity are Functions that map instances of ConstantQuantity to other instances of ConstantQuantity (e.g., TimeDependentQuantities are FunctionQuantities). Although the name and definition of PhysicalQuantity is borrowed from physics, PhysicalQuantities need not be material. Aside from the dimensions of length, time, velocity, etc., nonphysical dimensions such as currency are also possible. Accordingly, amounts of money would be instances of PhysicalQuantity. PhysicalQuantities are distinguished from Numbers by the fact that the former are associated with a dimension of measurement." SUMO: http://www.ontologyportal.org/

Description


"A Predicate is a sentence-forming Relation. Each tuple in the Relation is a finite, ordered sequence of objects. The fact that a particular tuple is an element of a Predicate is denoted by '(*predicate* arg_1 arg_2 .. arg_n)', where the arg_i are the objects so related. In the case of BinaryPredicates, the fact can be read as `arg_1 is *predicate* arg_2' or `a *predicate* of arg_1 is arg_2'." (SUMO)

Class: expo:Proposition   back to top

  • expo:Abstract
    • expo:Proposition
      • uo:Unit
      • expo:ExperimentalHypothesis

      • expo:FieldOfStudy
      • expo:Model
      • expo:Prcedure
      • expo:Requirements
      • expo:Variable
      • vhbieo:EperimentalFactor

Description


Propositions are Abstract entities that express a complete thought or a set of such thoughts. As an example, the formula ' (instance Yojo Cat)' expresses the Proposition that the entity named Yojo is an element of the Class of Cats. Note that propositions are not restricted to the content expressed by individual sentences of a Language. They may encompass the content expressed by theories, books, and even whole libraries. It is important to distinguish Propositions from the ContentBearingObjects that express them. A Proposition is a piece of information, e.g. that the cat is on the mat, but a ContentBearingObject is an Object that represents this information. A Proposition is an abstraction that may have multiple representations: strings, sounds, icons, etc. For example, the Proposition that the cat is on the mat is represented here as a string of graphical characters displayed on a monitor and/or printed on paper, but it can be represented by a sequence of sounds or by some non-latin alphabet or by some cryptographic form.
Reference: SUMO http://berkelium.teknowledge.com:8080/sigma/home.jsp

Inherits from (2):
expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

Property Range of:
expo:has_content

Implementation:

@prefix expo: <http://www.hozo.jp/owl/EXPOApr19/> .
@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

expo:Proposition a owl:Class ;
rdfs:label "Proposition" ;
rdfs:comment """
Propositions are Abstract entities that express a complete thought or a set of such thoughts. As an example, the formula ' (instance Yojo Cat)' expresses the Proposition that the entity named Yojo is an element of the Class of Cats. Note that propositions are not restricted to the content expressed by individual sentences of a Language. They may encompass the content expressed by theories, books, and even whole libraries. It is important to distinguish Propositions from the ContentBearingObjects that express them. A Proposition is a piece of information, e.g. that the cat is on the mat, but a ContentBearingObject is an Object that represents this information. A Proposition is an abstraction that may have multiple representations: strings, sounds, icons, etc. For example, the Proposition that the cat is on the mat is represented here as a string of graphical characters displayed on a monitor and/or printed on paper, but it can be represented by a sequence of sounds or by some non-latin alphabet or by some cryptographic form.
Reference: SUMO http://berkelium.teknowledge.com:8080/sigma/home.jsp
""" ;
rdfs:subClassOf expo:Abstract ;

expo:Relation .

Description


"The Class of relations. There are three kinds of Relation: Predicate, Function, and List. Predicates and Functions both denote sets of ordered n-tuples. The difference between these two Classes is that Predicates cover formula-forming operators, while Functions cover term-forming operators. A List, on the other hand, is a particular ordered n-tuple." (SUMO)

Description


A sequential design is an experimental design where a sample group size of experimental objects is not determined in advance. The experiment is continued until the moment when the results are conclusive according to predetermined degree of significance or non-significance.

Reference: Based on: Langley, R. Practical Statistics. David&Charles Ltd, Newton,1971.

Description


A target variable is an unknown variable of the domain model about which the experiment is designed to discover new knowledge.
- VBEO, literally, takes a target variable as dependent variable because an experiment needs to discover knowledge about the target variable.

Inherits from (4):
expo:Variable | expo:Proposition | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

Property Domain of:
vhbieo:associatedWithStateOf

Property Range of:
sosa:actsOnProperty | vhbieo:associatedWithTarget

Implementation:

@prefix expo: <http://www.hozo.jp/owl/EXPOApr19/> .
@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

expo:TargetVariable a owl:Class ;
rdfs:label "TargetVariable" ;
rdfs:comment """
A target variable is an unknown variable of the domain model about which the experiment is designed to discover new knowledge.
""",
"VBEO, literally, takes a target variable as dependent variable because an experiment needs to discover knowledge about the target variable." ;
rdfs:subClassOf expo:Variable .

Class: expo:TimePoint   back to top

  • expo:TimePosition
    • expo:TimePoint

NOTE expo:TimePoint is a leaf node.

Description


"An extensionless point on the universal timeline. The TimePoints at which Processes occur can be known with various degrees of precision and approximation, but conceptually TimePoints are point-like and not interval-like. That is, it doesn't make sense to talk about how long a TimePoint lasts." SUMO: http://www.ontologyportal.org/

"An extensionless point on the universal timeline. The TimePoints at which Processes occur can be known with various degrees of precision and approximation, but conceptually TimePoints are point-like and not interval-like. That is, it doesn't make sense to talk about how long a TimePoint lasts." SUMO: http://www.ontologyportal.org/

NOTE gbxml_:Area is a leaf node.

Description

Specifies the area of the space or building. This value should be equal to the area enclosed by the physical boundaries of the space, as defined by the intersection of the horizontal plane at the highest floor height and the volumetric model's vertical interior surface planes. Building area should be the sum of space areas whose PeopleNumber element values are greater than zero.

Inherits from (8):
gbxml:GeometricParameter | gbxml:BuildingParameter | gbxml:Building | expo:Plan | expo:Prcedure | expo:Proposition | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

Implementation:

@prefix gbxml: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntologySharedVocabulary.owl#> .
@prefix gbxml_: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntology.owl#> .
@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

gbxml_:Area a owl:Class ;
rdfs:comment "Specifies the area of the space or building. This value should be equal to the area enclosed by the physical boundaries of the space, as defined by the intersection of the horizontal plane at the highest floor height and the volumetric model's vertical interior surface planes. Building area should be the sum of space areas whose PeopleNumber element values are greater than zero." ;
rdfs:subClassOf gbxml:GeometricParameter .

Class: gbxml_:CartesianPoint   back to top

  • gbxml:GeometricParameter
    • gbxml_:CartesianPoint

NOTE gbxml_:CartesianPoint is a leaf node.

Description

This is the x, y, and z distances from the origin. This element must have three Coordinate elements when representing 3-d space, which represent x, y and z in order. This element must have two Coordinate elements when representing 2-d space.

Class: gbxml_:ImageTexture   back to top

  • gbxml:MaterialParameter
    • gbxml_:ImageTexture

NOTE gbxml_:ImageTexture is a leaf node.

Description

This is an X3D element to map a texture to this material. From X3D specification: The ImageTexture node defines a texture map by specifying an image file and general parameters for mapping to geometry. Texture maps are defined in a 2D coordinate system (s, t) that ranges from [0.0, 1.0] in both directions. The bottom edge of the image corresponds to the S-axis of the texture map, and left edge of the image corresponds to the T-axis of the texture map. The lower-left pixel of the image corresponds to s=0, t=0, and the top-right pixel of the image corresponds to s=1, t=1.

Inherits from (9):
gbxml:MaterialParameter | gbxml:StructureParameter | gbxml:BuildingParameter | gbxml:Building | expo:Plan | expo:Prcedure | expo:Proposition | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

Implementation:

@prefix gbxml: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntologySharedVocabulary.owl#> .
@prefix gbxml_: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntology.owl#> .
@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

gbxml_:ImageTexture a owl:Class ;
rdfs:comment """This is an X3D element to map a texture to this material. From X3D specification: The ImageTexture node defines a texture map by specifying an image file and general parameters for mapping to geometry. Texture maps are defined in a 2D coordinate system (s, t) that ranges from [0.0, 1.0] in both directions. The bottom edge of the image corresponds to the S-axis of the texture map, and left edge of the image corresponds to the T-axis of the texture map. The lower-left pixel of the image corresponds to s=0, t=0, and the top-right pixel of the image corresponds to s=1, t=1.
""" ;
rdfs:subClassOf gbxml:MaterialParameter .

Class: gbxml_:Location   back to top

  • gbxml:PositionParameter
    • gbxml_:Location

NOTE gbxml_:Location is a leaf node.

Description

The Location element describes the location of the global origin for this campus. This element can be used in a general sense by using the Name and Description elements for a physical address or landmark, or Location can be made precise by specifying the Elevation, Longitude, and Latitude of the origin.

Class: gbxml_:PhotometryOrientation   back to top

  • gbxml:GeometricParameter
    • gbxml_:PhotometryOrientation

NOTE gbxml_:PhotometryOrientation is a leaf node.

Description

This element specifies the position and the x, y and z axis of the light source. This element must have four Coordinate elements which represent the position and the x, y and z axis in order. The first CartesianPoint element specifies the position of the light source. The second, third and fourth CartesianPoint elements specifies the displacement points for the positive x, positive y and positive z axis.

Inherits from (8):
gbxml:GeometricParameter | gbxml:BuildingParameter | gbxml:Building | expo:Plan | expo:Prcedure | expo:Proposition | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

gbxml_:PhotometryOrientation a owl:Class ;
rdfs:comment "This element specifies the position and the x, y and z axis of the light source. Class: gbxml_:PlanarGeometry   back to top

  • gbxml:GeometricParameter
    • gbxml_:PlanarGeometry

NOTE gbxml_:PlanarGeometry is a leaf node.

Description

List of points defining a loop. There are no repeated points in the list. All data are global, with the assumption that positive Z is up, and if CADModelAzimuth is undefined or zero, positive X is East and positive Y is North. If CADModelAzimuth is defined it is the angle of positive Y to North, positive X is the vectorial product of Y and Z. If geometry is to be precise, use Longitude, Latitude and Elevation in the Location element to define the origin. Otherwise the origin is an arbitrary point. Use PlanarGeometry to define a three dimensional polygon that lies on a plane, and has no self-intersection.

Inherits from (8):
gbxml:GeometricParameter | gbxml:BuildingParameter | gbxml:Building | expo:Plan | expo:Prcedure | expo:Proposition | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

Implementation:

@prefix gbxml: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntologySharedVocabulary.owl#> .
@prefix gbxml_: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntology.owl#> .
@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

gbxml_:PlanarGeometry a owl:Class ;
rdfs:comment "List of points defining a loop. There are no repeated points in the list. All data are global, with the assumption that positive Z is up, and if CADModelAzimuth is undefined or zero, positive X is East and positive Y is North. If CADModelAzimuth is defined it is the angle of positive Y to North, positive X is the vectorial product of Y and Z. If geometry is to be precise, use Longitude, Latitude and Elevation in the Location element to define the origin. Otherwise the origin is an arbitrary point. Use PlanarGeometry to define a three dimensional polygon that lies on a plane, and has no self-intersection." ;
rdfs:subClassOf gbxml:GeometricParameter .

    • gbxml_:PointData

NOTE gbxml_:PointData is a leaf node.

Description

The PointData element allows for graph or tabular information to be entered. The data type and units of the independent and dependent variables are defined in their respective elements. Each Data element represent a data point, with each Value element representing the value of a variable - starting with the independent variable, then each dependent variable listed in the order defined.

Class: gbxml_:PolyLoop   back to top

  • gbxml:GeometricParameter
    • gbxml_:PolyLoop

NOTE gbxml_:PolyLoop is a leaf node.

Description

This is a list of coordinates that make up a polygon in three-dimensional space. All coordinates must lie on the same plane. The right-hand rule applies for defining the outward normal of a surface: For every surface, points must be defined in order, such that the direction of (the average cross-product between (any point, the centroid of the surface, and the next point)) points in the direction of the outward normal, which is a vector pointing away from the first AdjacentSpaceID listed.

Inherits from (8):
gbxml:GeometricParameter | gbxml:BuildingParameter | gbxml:Building | expo:Plan | expo:Prcedure | expo:Proposition | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

Implementation:

@prefix gbxml_: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntology.owl#> .
@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

gbxml_:PolyLoop a owl:Class ;
rdfs:comment "This is a list of coordinates that make up a polygon in three-dimensional space. All coordinates must lie on the same plane. The right-hand rule applies for defining the outward normal of a surface: For every surface, points must be defined in order, such that the direction of (the average cross-product between (any point, the centroid of the surface, and the next point)) points in the direction of the outward normal, which is a vector pointing away from the first AdjacentSpaceID listed." ;

Class: gbxml_:RectangularGeometry   back to top

  • gbxml:GeometricParameter
    • gbxml_:RectangularGeometry

NOTE gbxml_:RectangularGeometry is a leaf node.

Description

Geometry data in a form typically used in simulation engines. For surfaces, specify the location of the bottom-left corner with the CartesianPoint element when facing it from the outside. Also for surfaces, Tilt and Azimuth must be specified. If CADModelAzimuth is defined, the Azimuth value is relative to the CADModelAzimuth value rather then North. For openings, the third Coordinate should be zero or left missing. For openings, these Coordinates represent the distance of the bottom-left of the opening to the bottom-left corner of the parent surface. Azimuth and Tilt should not be specified for opening. There is an optional PolyLoop element, which may be used for describing the polygon shape of the surface.

Inherits from (8):
gbxml:GeometricParameter | gbxml:BuildingParameter | gbxml:Building | expo:Plan | expo:Prcedure | expo:Proposition | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

Implementation:

@prefix gbxml: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntologySharedVocabulary.owl#> .
@prefix gbxml_: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntology.owl#> .
@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

gbxml_:RectangularGeometry a owl:Class ;
rdfs:comment "Geometry data in a form typically used in simulation engines. For surfaces, specify the location of the bottom-left corner with the CartesianPoint element when facing it from the outside. Also for surfaces, Tilt and Azimuth must be specified. If CADModelAzimuth is defined, the Azimuth value is relative to the CADModelAzimuth value rather then North. For openings, the third Coordinate should be zero or left missing. For openings, these Coordinates represent the distance of the bottom-left of the opening to the bottom-left corner of the parent surface. Azimuth and Tilt should not be specified for opening. There is an optional PolyLoop element, which may be used for describing the polygon shape of the surface." ;
rdfs:subClassOf gbxml:GeometricParameter .

Class: gbxml_:ShellGeometry   back to top

  • gbxml:GeometricParameter
    • gbxml_:ShellGeometry

NOTE gbxml_:ShellGeometry is a leaf node.

Description

All data are global, with the assumption that positive Z is up, and if CADModelAzimuth is undefined or zero, positive X is East and positive Y is North. If CADModelAzimuth is defined it is the angle of positive Y to North, positive X is the vectorial product of Y and Z. If geometry is to be precise, use Longitude Latitude, and Elevation in the Location element to define the origin. Otherwise the origin is an arbitrary point. ShellGeometry is used to define a union of closed shells, where there is no intersection of any two of the given shells.

Inherits from (8):
gbxml:GeometricParameter | gbxml:BuildingParameter | gbxml:Building | expo:Plan | expo:Prcedure | expo:Proposition | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

Implementation:

@prefix gbxml: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntologySharedVocabulary.owl#> .
@prefix gbxml_: <https://www.auto.tuwien.ac.at/downloads/thinkhome/ontology/BuildingOntology.owl#> .
@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

gbxml_:ShellGeometry a owl:Class ;
rdfs:comment "All data are global, with the assumption that positive Z is up, and if CADModelAzimuth is undefined or zero, positive X is East and positive Y is North. If CADModelAzimuth is defined it is the angle of positive Y to North, positive X is the vectorial product of Y and Z. If geometry is to be precise, use Longitude Latitude, and Elevation in the Location element to define the origin. Otherwise the origin is an arbitrary point. ShellGeometry is used to define a union of closed shells, where there is no intersection of any two of the given shells." ;
rdfs:subClassOf gbxml:GeometricParameter .

Class: gbxml_:WindowType   back to top

  • gbxml:MaterialParameter
    • gbxml_:WindowType

NOTE gbxml_:WindowType is a leaf node.

Description

One WindowType should be created for each type of window. Create a Blind, Frame, and Cost for each OpeningType, and then add as many Glaze and Gaps as exist in the window. Place these Glaze and Gap elements in order from outside to inside. For instance, a two pane window will have Glaze Gap Glaze, where the first Glaze represents the outside surface.

Inherits from (9):
gbxml:MaterialParameter | gbxml:StructureParameter | gbxml:BuildingParameter | gbxml:Building | expo:Plan | expo:Prcedure | expo:Proposition | expo:Abstract | expo:Entity

@prefix owl: <http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#> .
@prefix rdfs: <http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#> .

gbxml_:WindowType a owl:Class ;
rdfs:comment "One WindowType should be created for each type of window. Create a Blind, Frame, and Cost for each OpeningType, and then add as many Glaze and Gaps as exist in the window. Place these Glaze and Gap elements in order from outside to inside. For instance, a two pane window will have Glaze Gap Glaze, where the first Glaze represents the outside surface." ;
rdfs:subClassOf gbxml:MaterialParameter .
